## File: psappdeploytoolkit.com_docs_3.10.2_examples_googlechrome-configmgr.md

---
url: "https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/examples/googlechrome-configmgr"
title: "MCM - Google Chrome · PSAppDeployToolkit"
---

[Skip to main content](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/examples/googlechrome-configmgr#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

This is documentation for PSAppDeployToolkit **3.10.2 (Deprecated)**, which is no longer actively maintained.

For up-to-date documentation, see the **[latest version](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/examples/googlechrome-configmgr)** (4.1.0).

Version: 3.10.2 (Deprecated)

On this page

## Introduction [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/examples/googlechrome-configmgr\#introduction "Direct link to Introduction")

In this example, we will build a Google Chrome Enterprise deployment which provides the following benefits over using the standard MSI based deployment:

- The ability to defer the installation up to 3 times
- The ability to close any applications that could cause errors during the installation
- Verification that the required disk space is available
- Full removal of any previous version of Google Chrome, both consumer and enterprise versions (to prevent issues sometimes seen when doing an MSI upgrade, i.e. Missing previous installation source files)

## Creating the PSAppDeployToolkit deployment [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/examples/googlechrome-configmgr\#creating-the-psappdeploytoolkit-deployment "Direct link to Creating the PSAppDeployToolkit deployment")

- Start with a fresh copy of the PSAppDeployToolkit source files.

![Google Chrome installation Files](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/assets/images/chrome-sccm20-51c8929f265fec2d8f3bc1f93740fbda.png)

- Download and copy the Google Chrome Enterprise MSI file in to the `Files` folder, e.g.

![Google Chrome installation Files](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/assets/images/chrome-sccm20-51c8929f265fec2d8f3bc1f93740fbda.png)

### Script Customization [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/examples/googlechrome-configmgr\#script-customization "Direct link to Script Customization")

Open the `Deploy-Application.ps1` script and customize with the following changes:

#### Initialization [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/examples/googlechrome-configmgr\#initialization "Direct link to Initialization")

Populate these variables with the application and script details:

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
$appVendor = 'Google'
$appName = 'Chrome Enterprise (x64)'
$appVersion = '118.0.5993.118'
$appArch = 'x64'
$appLang = 'EN'
$appRevision = '01'
$appScriptVersion = '1.0.0'
$appScriptDate = '10/31/2023'
$appScriptAuthor = 'Dan Cunningham'

```

#### Pre-Install [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/examples/googlechrome-configmgr\#pre-install "Direct link to Pre-Install")

Copy the following into the Pre-Install section:

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
## Prompt the user to close the following applications if they are running and
## allow the option to defer the installation up to 3 times:
Show-InstallationWelcome -CloseApps 'chrome' -AllowDefer -DeferTimes 3

## Show Progress Message (with the default message)
Show-InstallationProgress

## Remove any previous versions of Google Chrome (consumer and enterprise)
Remove-MSIApplications -Name 'Google Chrome'

```

#### Installation [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/examples/googlechrome-configmgr\#installation "Direct link to Installation")

Copy the following into the Installation section:

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
## Install the MSI
Execute-MSI -Action Install -Path 'googlechromestandaloneenterprisex64.msi'

```

#### Post-Installation [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/examples/googlechrome-configmgr\#post-installation "Direct link to Post-Installation")

Copy the following into the Post-Install section:

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
## No actions required here

```

#### Uninstallation [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/examples/googlechrome-configmgr\#uninstallation "Direct link to Uninstallation")

Copy the following into the Uninstallation section:

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
## Prompt the user to close the following applications if they are running:
Show-InstallationWelcome -CloseApps 'chrome'

## Show Progress Message (with a message to indicate the application is being uninstalled)
Show-InstallationProgress -StatusMessage "Uninstalling Application $installTitle. Please Wait..."

## Remove this version of Google Chrome Enterprise
Execute-MSI -Action Uninstall -Path '{3ACBC599-F9FA-344F-A90C-4BC47885D629}'

```

### Testing the Deployment Script [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/examples/googlechrome-configmgr\#testing-the-deployment-script "Direct link to Testing the Deployment Script")

- Install the application by running the following from a Windows Powershell command prompt:

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
.\Deploy-Application.ps1

```

or

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
.\Deploy-Application.ps1 -DeploymentType Install

```

- Uninstall the application by running:

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
.\Deploy-Application.ps1 -DeploymentType Uninstall

```

* * *

## Deploying through MCM using the Application Model [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/examples/googlechrome-configmgr\#deploying-through-mcm-using-the-application-model "Direct link to Deploying through MCM using the Application Model")

### Creating the Application [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/examples/googlechrome-configmgr\#creating-the-application "Direct link to Creating the Application")

- Copy the installation files to your application sources folder. This should be a network share accessible by your Microsoft Configuration Manager Primary Site.

- Within the Configuration Manager Console, create a new Application:


![MCM Create Application](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/assets/images/chrome-sccm3-284254ecf43c7cf6024497a115854d3b.png)

- Manually specify the application information:

![MCM Select manually specify the application information](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/assets/images/chrome-sccm4-84c66557116a36c03a3ec21b615abdc3.png)

![MCM Manually specify the application information](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/assets/images/chrome-sccm5-52ba9598646244db7d50961de419e785.png)

- Specify the Software Center entry details:

![MCM Specify the Software Center entry details](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/assets/images/chrome-sccm6-2a17eb8983c247f295b32bdbf6b7a519.png)

### Creating the Deployment Type [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/examples/googlechrome-configmgr\#creating-the-deployment-type "Direct link to Creating the Deployment Type")

- Add a Deployment Type:

![MCM Add a Deployment Type](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/assets/images/chrome-sccm7-9c028df8c28b201cde9e61f5eb0ba599.png)

- Add a type of Script Installer:

![MCM Add a type of Script Installer](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/assets/images/chrome-sccm8-6e700d2617cd337e8c78cd99868e7aec.png)

![MCM Specify general information for this Deployment Type](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/assets/images/chrome-sccm9-5bf11e2c8c5486c9d65ba1cb2e1fc71d.png)

- Specify the Content Details. Ensure the content location is set correctly and tick Persist content in the client cache.

- Enter the following for the Installation program:


```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Powershell.exe -File Deploy-Application.ps1

```

- Enter the following for the Uninstall program:

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Powershell.exe -File Deploy-Application.ps1 -DeploymentType Uninstall

```

![MCM Specify the content location for this Deployment Type](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/assets/images/chrome-sccm10-1c8f487db532ebbf9419c0af55882dc2.png)

- For the Deployment Type Detection Method, add a Clause. Select Windows Installer and browse for the MSI file. This should populate the product code automatically:

![MCM Deployment Type Detection Method](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/assets/images/chrome-sccm12-5c0230d1537154be1e8c96830463cbde.png)

![MCM Deployment Type Detection Clause](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/assets/images/chrome-sccm13-2be0ab9c22f35351ac2ee4c336085a1e.png)

- For the Deployment Type User Experience, select Install for User, Installation program visibility to Normal, and select the checkbox to allow users to view and interact with the program installation.

- Click Next on the Deployment Type Requirements page.


![MCM Deployment Type Requirements](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/assets/images/chrome-sccm15-9d0fccae60cfa9a5c21a5faa9759a29a.png)

- Click Next on the Dependencies page.

![MCM Deployment Type Dependencies](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/assets/images/chrome-sccm16-900accaf6113c0f3cda667178bf6866b.png)

- Click Next on the Deployment Type Summary page.

![MCM Deployment Type Summary](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/assets/images/chrome-sccm17-982461fce19df20064ff5cb82854836e.png)

- Click Close on the Deployment Type Completion page.

![MCM Deployment Type Completion](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/assets/images/chrome-sccm18-10b16e5dff6728f7ce608d24e0cab0ed.png)

- Click Next on the Deployment Type page.

![MCM Deployment Type](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/assets/images/chrome-sccm19-8b5a4b93ae58221e829355c0e79d89de.png)

- Click Next on the Application Summary page.

![MCM Application Summary](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/assets/images/chrome-sccm20-51c8929f265fec2d8f3bc1f93740fbda.png)

- Click Close on the Application Completion page.

![MCM Application Completion](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/assets/images/chrome-sccm21-4c8fe45098f35e4a0c16f0d14d54bbdd.png)

### Deploying the Application [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/examples/googlechrome-configmgr\#deploying-the-application "Direct link to Deploying the Application")

- Right click on the Application and select Deploy:

![MCM Deploy Application](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/assets/images/chrome-sccm22-0ccc79b2b9406dcc11d6dcabffc1ad7e.png)

- Select the collection to deploy to and click Next to start the deployment.

### Testing the Application [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/examples/googlechrome-configmgr\#testing-the-application "Direct link to Testing the Application")

- Within a few minutes, you should see the application available for install in Software Center:

![MCM Software Center App](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/assets/images/chrome-sccm23-b0c509f965dbb4d803e0adb31efae629.png)

![MCM Software Center App Details](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/assets/images/chrome-sccm24-553fe7db34a2ff6f3b93f1ba441859f5.png)

- Select Install to start the installation.

- The installation will now start. When complete, the Status should change to Installed:


![MCM Software Center App Complete](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/assets/images/chrome-sccm25-17656603ea69b018fbdfe84719921025.png)

- You can use the PSAppDeployToolkit automatic logging, including the Windows Installer logs by navigating to the logs folder (default is C:\\Windows\\Logs\\Software):

![MCM PSAppDeployToolkit Logs](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/assets/images/chrome-sccm26-638cec98a368db38e9eb497c57ab7182.png)

- [Introduction](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/examples/googlechrome-configmgr#introduction)
- [Creating the PSAppDeployToolkit deployment](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/examples/googlechrome-configmgr#creating-the-psappdeploytoolkit-deployment)
- [Deploying through MCM using the Application Model](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/examples/googlechrome-configmgr#deploying-through-mcm-using-the-application-model)

## File: psappdeploytoolkit.com_docs_3.10.2_exit-codes.md

---
url: "https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/exit-codes"
title: "Exit Codes · PSAppDeployToolkit"
---

[Skip to main content](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/exit-codes#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

This is documentation for PSAppDeployToolkit **3.10.2 (Deprecated)**, which is no longer actively maintained.

For up-to-date documentation, see the **[latest version](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/reference/exit-codes)** (4.1.0).

Version: 3.10.2 (Deprecated)

PSAppDeployToolkit uses pre-defined Exit Codes to indicate the success or failure of a deployment and can be used to control the flow of your deployment logic, or just to understand what happened during a deployment.

| Exit Code | Description |
| --- | --- |
| 60000 - 68999 | Reserved for built-in exit codes in _Deploy-Application.ps1_, _Deploy-Application.exe_, and _AppDeployToolkitMain.ps1_. |
| 69000 - 69999 | Recommended for user customized exit codes in `Deploy-Application.ps1`. |
| 70000 - 79999 | Recommended for user customized exit codes in `Deploy-Application.ps1`. |
| 60001 | An error occurred in `Deploy-Application.ps1`. Check your script syntax use. |
| 60002 | Error when running `Execute-Process` function. |
| 60003 | Administrator privileges required for `Execute-ProcessAsUser` function. |
| 60004 | Failure when loading .NET Winforms / WPF Assemblies. |
| 60005 | Failure when displaying the Blocked Application dialog. |
| 60006 | AllowSystemInteractionFallback option was not selected in the config XML file, so toolkit will not fall back to SYSTEM context with no interaction. |
| 60007 | `Deploy-Application.ps1` failed to dot source `AppDeployToolkitMain.ps1` either because it could not be found or there was an error while it was being dot sourced. |
| 60008 | The `-UserName` parameter in the `Execute-ProcessAsUser` function has a default value that is empty because no logged in users were detected when the toolkit was launched. |
| 60009 | `Deploy-Application.exe` failed before _PowerShell.exe_ process could be launched. |
| 60010 | `Deploy-Application.exe` failed before PowerShell.exe process could be launched. |
| 60011 | `Deploy-Application.exe` failed to execute the PowerShell.exe process. |
| 60012 | A UI prompt timed out or the user opted to defer the installation. |
| 60013 | If `Execute-Process` function captures an exit code out of range for int32 then return this custom exit code. |

---

## File: psappdeploytoolkit.com_docs_3.10.2_getting-started_download.md

---
url: "https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/getting-started/download"
title: "Downloading · PSAppDeployToolkit"
---

[Skip to main content](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/getting-started/download#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

This is documentation for PSAppDeployToolkit **3.10.2 (Deprecated)**, which is no longer actively maintained.

For up-to-date documentation, see the **[latest version](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/introduction)** (4.1.0).

Version: 3.10.2 (Deprecated)

On this page

## Downloading PSAppDeployToolkit [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/getting-started/download\#downloading-psappdeploytoolkit "Direct link to Downloading PSAppDeployToolkit")

PSAppDeployToolkit is provided as a self-contained Zip file archive, which contains the logic-engine and supporting PSFunctions for you to leverage, as well as a standardized deployment template. You can paste the following PowerShell code into a PowerShell console window to automatically download and extract the latest version of PSAppDeployToolkit to your user profile's Downloads folder.

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
## Download the latest release of PSAppDeployToolkit from GitHub
$githubRepository = "psappdeploytoolkit/psappdeploytoolkit"
$filenamePatternMatch = "PSAppDeployToolkit*.zip"
$psadtReleaseUri = "https://api.github.com/repos/$githubRepository/releases/latest"
$psadtDownloadUri = ((Invoke-RestMethod -Method GET -Uri $psadtReleaseUri).assets | Where-Object name -like $filenamePatternMatch ).browser_download_url
$zipExtractionPath = Join-Path $env:USERPROFILE "Downloads" "PSAppDeployToolkit"
$zipTempDownloadPath = Join-Path -Path $([System.IO.Path]::GetTempPath()) -ChildPath $(Split-Path -Path $psadtDownloadUri -Leaf)

## Download to a temporary folder
Invoke-WebRequest -Uri $psadtDownloadUri -Out $zipTempDownloadPath
## Remove any Zone.Identifier alternate data streams to unblock the file (if required)
Unblock-File -Path $zipTempDownloadPath
## Extract the contents of the zip file to a subfolder under the current user's Downloads folder
Expand-Archive -Path $zipTempDownloadPath -DestinationPath $zipExtractionPath -Force

Write-Host ("File: {0} extracted to Path: {1}" -f $psadtDownloadUri, $zipExtractionPath) -ForegroundColor Yellow

```

Alternatively, you can download and extract yourself from here:

- [PSAppDeployToolkit Latest Release](https://github.com/PSAppDeployToolkit/PSAppDeployToolkit/releases/latest).

Once extracted, you will see a file and folder structure similar to the one outlined on the next page.

## Why is PSAppDeployToolkit not a PowerShell module? [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/getting-started/download\#why-is-psappdeploytoolkit-not-a-powershell-module "Direct link to Why is PSAppDeployToolkit not a PowerShell module?")

PSAppDeployToolkit is not a PowerShell module, and this was a very deliberate decision made early on. For a number of reasons, we wanted to avoid the need to install PSAppDeployToolkit on the target system. :

- PSAppDeployToolkit is a PowerShell-based logic engine that is used to drive application deployments en-masse in an enterprise environment.
- PowerShell modules are installed on the endpoint and can be scoped to the Current User or Local Machine, either for Windows PowerShell or PowerShell Core.

If PSAppDeployToolkit was decoupled from the deployment script and instead, installed & updated as a module we would immediately run into a number of issues:

- Before deploying any application in a production environment, you should always test against a handful of endpoints, fix any issues encountered and repeat the process until the deployment script has been thoroughly tested to ensure no bugs, typos etc. Most large environments require a Change Management process to be followed with testing and validation results.
- A change in PSADT module version, either automated or manually initiated, would invalidate testing of any previous software deployment script.
- The version of the PSADT module installed on the endpoint might not be the same as the version used to create and test the deployment package. This means your testing is unlikely to be 100% reliably against what is actually deployed in your environment.
- Depending on how the module was deployed and whether it is currently in-use, the standard Remove-Module and Update-Module commands can fail.
- A change in module version would introduce the requirement of ensuring all PSFunction and Parameter names, as well as their expect output did not change between versions, tying our hands for certain types of easy enhancements and fixes.

For these reasons, we recommend that you use the PSAppDeployToolkit standalone package provided on GitHub, and not rely on the module that is currently listed on the PowerShell Gallery.

- [Downloading PSAppDeployToolkit](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/getting-started/download#downloading-psappdeploytoolkit)
- [Why is PSAppDeployToolkit not a PowerShell module?](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/getting-started/download#why-is-psappdeploytoolkit-not-a-powershell-module)

---

## File: psappdeploytoolkit.com_docs_3.10.2_getting-started_requirements.md

---
url: "https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/getting-started/requirements"
title: "Requirements · PSAppDeployToolkit"
---

[Skip to main content](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/getting-started/requirements#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

This is documentation for PSAppDeployToolkit **3.10.2 (Deprecated)**, which is no longer actively maintained.

For up-to-date documentation, see the **[latest version](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/getting-started/requirements)** (4.1.0).

Version: 3.10.2 (Deprecated)

On this page

## PowerShell Version [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/getting-started/requirements\#powershell-version "Direct link to PowerShell Version")

PSAppDeployToolkit have been tested against PowerShell versions as far back as PowerShell 2.0. However, for performance and stablilty (as well as supportability), we recommend using the latest version of PowerShell version available for your operating system.

## Windows Client [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/getting-started/requirements\#windows-client "Direct link to Windows Client")

### Currently Supported [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/getting-started/requirements\#currently-supported "Direct link to Currently Supported")

PSAppDeployToolkit 3.x is primarily developed on the latest Windows Client operating system (currently Windows 11) and we aim to test and validate against any versions on the list of [Microsoft's currently supported Windows Client versions](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/release-health/supported-versions-windows-client).

- Windows 11 24H2
- Windows 11 22H2
- Windows 11 21H2
- Windows 10 22H2
- Windows 10 21H2
- Windows 10 1809

### Best Effort Support [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/getting-started/requirements\#best-effort-support "Direct link to Best Effort Support")

The lifecycle of Enterprise devices are often driven be external factors affecting budgets - and often require IT teams to maintain devices that are no longer supported by Microsoft. And so, while we can't guarantee PSAppDeployToolkit will work on older operating systems, we periodically test against operating system versions that are no longer supported by Microsoft. The following have been tested and verified as working:

- Windows 10 1607 (Extended Support)
- Windows 10 1507 (RTM) (Extended Support)
- Windows 8.1
- Windows 7

## Windows Server [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/getting-started/requirements\#windows-server "Direct link to Windows Server")

### Currently Supported [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/getting-started/requirements\#currently-supported-1 "Direct link to Currently Supported")

Additionally, we test and validate against the Long-Term Servicing Channel (LTSC) versions on the list of [Microsoft's currently supported Windows Server list](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/release-health/windows-server-release-info).

- Windows Server 2022

### Best Effort Support [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/getting-started/requirements\#best-effort-support-1 "Direct link to Best Effort Support")

The lifecycle of Enterprise devices are often driven be external factors affecting budgets - and often require IT teams to maintain devices that are no longer supported by Microsoft. And so, while we can't guarantee PSAppDeployToolkit will work on older operating systems, we periodically test against operating system versions that are are no longer supported by Microsoft. The following have been tested and verified as working:

- Windows Server 2019 (version 1809)
- Windows Server 2016 (version 1606)
- Windows Server 2012 R2
- Windows Server 2008 R2

## Older Windows Versions [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/getting-started/requirements\#older-windows-versions "Direct link to Older Windows Versions")

While we have attempted to maintain this backwards compatibility through the life cycle of PSAppDeployToolkit, the degree of testing performed across older Operating Systems such as XP and Vista is limited. However, PSAppDeployToolkit has widespread adoption in the enterprise from SMEs to large multinationals so there is safety in numbers and the assurance that PSAppDeployToolkit has been put through its paces VERY extensively on a large number of Windows clients around the globe.

- [PowerShell Version](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/getting-started/requirements#powershell-version)
- [Windows Client](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/getting-started/requirements#windows-client)
- [Windows Server](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/getting-started/requirements#windows-server)
- [Older Windows Versions](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/getting-started/requirements#older-windows-versions)

---

## File: psappdeploytoolkit.com_docs_3.10.2_introduction.md

---
url: "https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/introduction"
title: "Introduction · PSAppDeployToolkit"
---

[Skip to main content](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/introduction#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

This is documentation for PSAppDeployToolkit **3.10.2 (Deprecated)**, which is no longer actively maintained.

For up-to-date documentation, see the **[latest version](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/introduction)** (4.1.0).

Version: 3.10.2 (Deprecated)

On this page

PSAppDeployToolkit is a framework for deploying applications in a business / corporate environment. It provides a set of well-defined functions for common application deployment tasks, as well as user interface elements for end user interaction during a deployment. It simplifies the complex scripting challenges of deploying applications in the enterprise, provides a consistent deployment experience for your end users and as a result of this, improves the overall success rate of your deployments.

In this documentation, you'll find information on the features and benefits of PSAppDeployToolkit, its system requirements and support, as well as instructions for downloading and deploying applications using the toolkit.

## Open-source & Contributing [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/introduction\#open-source--contributing "Direct link to Open-source & Contributing")

PSAppDeployToolkit is an open-source project (see [`LICENSE`](https://github.com/psappdeploytoolkit/psappdeploytoolkit/blob/master/LICENSE) file for more information). The core project, as well as the documentation and any related tools can be found in the [PSAppDeployToolkit](https://github.com/psappdeploytoolkit) GitHub organization.

PSAppDeployToolkit is open to code contributions and the PSAppDeployToolkit team appreciates every contribution, be it a feature request, bug report, or pull request.

info

Want to join the community?
You can join [GitHub](https://github.com/psappdeploytoolkit/psappdeploytoolkit), the [Forum](https://discourse.psappdeploytoolkit.com/), or the [#psappdeploytoolkit channel on Discord](https://discord.com/channels/618712310185197588/627204361545842688) to share your ideas and opinions with other community members and the PSAppDeployToolkit team. If you're looking for news and updates about PSAppDeployToolkit, [Twitter](https://twitter.com/psappdeploytoolkitjs) and the [blog](https://psappdeploytoolkit.io/blog) are pretty good places to start!

## Support [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/introduction\#support "Direct link to Support")

PSAppDeployToolkit is offered as free and open-source for users who wish to use it. When having an issue or a question, the [forum](https://discourse.psappdeploytoolkit.com/), or the [#psappdeploytoolkit channel on Discord](https://discord.com/channels/618712310185197588/627204361545842688) are great places to reach out for help. Both the PSAppDeployToolkit community and core developers often check this platform and answer posts.

## Something missing? [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/introduction\#something-missing "Direct link to Something missing?")

If you find issues with the documentation or have suggestions on how to improve the documentation or the project in general, please [file an issue](https://github.com/PSAppDeployToolkit/PSAppDeployToolkit/issues) for us.

- [Open-source & Contributing](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/introduction#open-source--contributing)
- [Support](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/introduction#support)
- [Something missing?](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/introduction#something-missing)

## File: psappdeploytoolkit.com_docs_3.10.2_reference.md

---
url: "https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference"
title: "Reference · PSAppDeployToolkit"
---

[Skip to main content](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

This is documentation for PSAppDeployToolkit **3.10.2 (Deprecated)**, which is no longer actively maintained.

For up-to-date documentation, see the **[latest version](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/reference)** (4.1.0).

Version: 3.10.2 (Deprecated)

On this page

PSAppDeployToolkit uses pre-defined **Exit Codes** to indicate the success or failure of a deployment and can be used to control the flow of your deployment logic, or just to understand what happened during a deployment.

For script development, PSAppDeployToolkit defines a wide range of **Variables** and **Functions** which you can use to speed up your deployment, simplify your scripting, and make your life easier.

You can find the full list of Exit Codes, Variables and Functions in the sidebar to the left. You can also use the search bar at the top of the page.

## File: psappdeploytoolkit.com_docs_3.10.2_reference_functions_Block-AppExecution.md

---
url: "https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Block-AppExecution"
title: "Block-AppExecution · PSAppDeployToolkit"
---

[Skip to main content](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Block-AppExecution#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

This is documentation for PSAppDeployToolkit **3.10.2 (Deprecated)**, which is no longer actively maintained.

For up-to-date documentation, see the **[latest version](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/introduction)** (4.1.0).

Version: 3.10.2 (Deprecated)

On this page

## SYNOPSIS [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Block-AppExecution\#synopsis "Direct link to SYNOPSIS")

Block the execution of an application(s)

## SYNTAX [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Block-AppExecution\#syntax "Direct link to SYNTAX")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Block-AppExecution [-ProcessName] <String[]> [<CommonParameters>]

```

## DESCRIPTION [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Block-AppExecution\#description "Direct link to DESCRIPTION")

This function is called when you pass the -BlockExecution parameter to the Stop-RunningApplications function.
It does the following:

1. Makes a copy of this script in a temporary directory on the local machine.
2. Checks for an existing scheduled task from previous failed installation attempt where apps were blocked and if found, calls the Unblock-AppExecution function to restore the original IFEO registry keys.
This is to prevent the function from overriding the backup of the original IFEO options.
3. Creates a scheduled task to restore the IFEO registry key values in case the script is terminated uncleanly by calling the local temporary copy of this script with the parameter -CleanupBlockedApps.
4. Modifies the "Image File Execution Options" registry key for the specified process(s) to call this script with the parameter -ShowBlockedAppDialog.
5. When the script is called with those parameters, it will display a custom message to the user to indicate that execution of the application has been blocked while the installation is in progress.
The text of this message can be customized in the XML configuration file.

## EXAMPLES [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Block-AppExecution\#examples "Direct link to EXAMPLES")

### EXAMPLE 1 [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Block-AppExecution\#example-1 "Direct link to EXAMPLE 1")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Block-AppExecution -ProcessName ('winword','excel')

```

## PARAMETERS [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Block-AppExecution\#parameters "Direct link to PARAMETERS")

### -ProcessName [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Block-AppExecution\#-processname "Direct link to -ProcessName")

Name of the process or processes separated by commas

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Type: String[]
Parameter Sets: (All)
Aliases:

Required: True
Position: 1
Default value: None
Accept pipeline input: False
Accept wildcard characters: False

```

### CommonParameters [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Block-AppExecution\#commonparameters "Direct link to CommonParameters")

This cmdlet supports the common parameters: -Debug, -ErrorAction, -ErrorVariable, -InformationAction, -InformationVariable, -OutVariable, -OutBuffer, -PipelineVariable, -Verbose, -WarningAction, and -WarningVariable. For more information, see [about\_CommonParameters](https://go.microsoft.com/fwlink/?LinkID=113216).

## INPUTS [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Block-AppExecution\#inputs "Direct link to INPUTS")

### None [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Block-AppExecution\#none "Direct link to None")

### You cannot pipe objects to this function. [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Block-AppExecution\#you-cannot-pipe-objects-to-this-function "Direct link to You cannot pipe objects to this function.")

## OUTPUTS [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Block-AppExecution\#outputs "Direct link to OUTPUTS")

### None [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Block-AppExecution\#none-1 "Direct link to None")

### This function does not generate any output. [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Block-AppExecution\#this-function-does-not-generate-any-output "Direct link to This function does not generate any output.")

## NOTES [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Block-AppExecution\#notes "Direct link to NOTES")

This is an internal script function and should typically not be called directly.

It is used when the -BlockExecution parameter is specified with the Show-InstallationWelcome function to block applications.

## File: psappdeploytoolkit.com_docs_3.10.2_reference_functions_Configure-EdgeExtension.md

---
url: "https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Configure-EdgeExtension"
title: "Configure-EdgeExtension · PSAppDeployToolkit"
---

[Skip to main content](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Configure-EdgeExtension#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

This is documentation for PSAppDeployToolkit **3.10.2 (Deprecated)**, which is no longer actively maintained.

For up-to-date documentation, see the **[latest version](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/introduction)** (4.1.0).

Version: 3.10.2 (Deprecated)

On this page

## SYNOPSIS [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Configure-EdgeExtension\#synopsis "Direct link to SYNOPSIS")

Configures an extension for Microsoft Edge using the ExtensionSettings policy

## SYNTAX [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Configure-EdgeExtension\#syntax "Direct link to SYNTAX")

### Add [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Configure-EdgeExtension\#add "Direct link to Add")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Configure-EdgeExtension [-Add] -ExtensionID <String> -InstallationMode <String> -UpdateUrl <String>
 [-MinimumVersionRequired <String>] [<CommonParameters>]

```

### Remove [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Configure-EdgeExtension\#remove "Direct link to Remove")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Configure-EdgeExtension [-Remove] -ExtensionID <String> [<CommonParameters>]

```

## DESCRIPTION [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Configure-EdgeExtension\#description "Direct link to DESCRIPTION")

This function configures an extension for Microsoft Edge using the ExtensionSettings policy: [https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/deployedge/microsoft-edge-manage-extensions-ref-guide](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/deployedge/microsoft-edge-manage-extensions-ref-guide)
This enables Edge Extensions to be installed and managed like applications, enabling extensions to be pushed to specific devices or users alongside existing GPO/Intune extension policies.
This should not be used in conjunction with Edge Management Service which leverages the same registry key to configure Edge extensions.

## EXAMPLES [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Configure-EdgeExtension\#examples "Direct link to EXAMPLES")

### EXAMPLE 1 [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Configure-EdgeExtension\#example-1 "Direct link to EXAMPLE 1")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Configure-EdgeExtension -Add -ExtensionID "extensionID" -InstallationMode "force_installed" -UpdateUrl "https://edge.microsoft.com/extensionwebstorebase/v1/crx"

```

### EXAMPLE 2 [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Configure-EdgeExtension\#example-2 "Direct link to EXAMPLE 2")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Configure-EdgeExtension -Remove -ExtensionID "extensionID"

```

## PARAMETERS [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Configure-EdgeExtension\#parameters "Direct link to PARAMETERS")

## File: psappdeploytoolkit.com_docs_3.10.2_reference_functions_Convert-RegistryPath.md

---
url: "https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Convert-RegistryPath"
title: "Convert-RegistryPath · PSAppDeployToolkit"
---

[Skip to main content](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Convert-RegistryPath#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

This is documentation for PSAppDeployToolkit **3.10.2 (Deprecated)**, which is no longer actively maintained.

For up-to-date documentation, see the **[latest version](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/introduction)** (4.1.0).

Version: 3.10.2 (Deprecated)

On this page

## SYNOPSIS [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Convert-RegistryPath\#synopsis "Direct link to SYNOPSIS")

Converts the specified registry key path to a format that is compatible with built-in PowerShell cmdlets.

## SYNTAX [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Convert-RegistryPath\#syntax "Direct link to SYNTAX")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Convert-RegistryPath [-Key] <String> [-Wow6432Node] [[-SID] <String>] [[-DisableFunctionLogging] <Boolean>]
 [<CommonParameters>]

```

## DESCRIPTION [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Convert-RegistryPath\#description "Direct link to DESCRIPTION")

Converts the specified registry key path to a format that is compatible with built-in PowerShell cmdlets.

Converts registry key hives to their full paths.
Example: HKLM is converted to "Registry::HKEY\_LOCAL\_MACHINE".

## EXAMPLES [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Convert-RegistryPath\#examples "Direct link to EXAMPLES")

### EXAMPLE 1 [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Convert-RegistryPath\#example-1 "Direct link to EXAMPLE 1")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Convert-RegistryPath -Key 'HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Uninstall\{1AD147D0-BE0E-3D6C-AC11-64F6DC4163F1}'

```

### EXAMPLE 2 [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Convert-RegistryPath\#example-2 "Direct link to EXAMPLE 2")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Convert-RegistryPath -Key 'HKLM:SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Uninstall\{1AD147D0-BE0E-3D6C-AC11-64F6DC4163F1}'

```

## PARAMETERS [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Convert-RegistryPath\#parameters "Direct link to PARAMETERS")

### -Key [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Convert-RegistryPath\#-key "Direct link to -Key")

Path to the registry key to convert (can be a registry hive or fully qualified path)

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Type: String
Parameter Sets: (All)
Aliases:

Required: True
Position: 1
Default value: None
Accept pipeline input: False
Accept wildcard characters: False

```

### -Wow6432Node [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Convert-RegistryPath\#-wow6432node "Direct link to -Wow6432Node")

Specifies that the 32-bit registry view (Wow6432Node) should be used on a 64-bit system.

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Type: SwitchParameter
Parameter Sets: (All)
Aliases:

Required: False
Position: Named
Default value: False
Accept pipeline input: False
Accept wildcard characters: False

```

### -SID [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Convert-RegistryPath\#-sid "Direct link to -SID")

The security identifier (SID) for a user.
Specifying this parameter will convert a HKEY\_CURRENT\_USER registry key to the HKEY\_USERS$SID format.

Specify this parameter from the Invoke-HKCURegistrySettingsForAllUsers function to read/edit HKCU registry settings for all users on the system.

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Type: String
Parameter Sets: (All)
Aliases:

Required: False
Position: 2
Default value: None
Accept pipeline input: False
Accept wildcard characters: False

```

### -DisableFunctionLogging [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Convert-RegistryPath\#-disablefunctionlogging "Direct link to -DisableFunctionLogging")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M

Parameter Sets: (All)

Required: False
Position: 3
Default value: True
Accept pipeline input: False
Accept wildcard characters: False

```

### CommonParameters [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Convert-RegistryPath\#commonparameters "Direct link to CommonParameters")

## File: psappdeploytoolkit.com_docs_3.10.2_reference_functions_ConvertTo-NTAccountOrSID.md

title: "ConvertTo-NTAccountOrSID · PSAppDeployToolkit"
---

[Skip to main content](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/ConvertTo-NTAccountOrSID#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

This is documentation for PSAppDeployToolkit **3.10.2 (Deprecated)**, which is no longer actively maintained.

For up-to-date documentation, see the **[latest version](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/introduction)** (4.1.0).

Version: 3.10.2 (Deprecated)

On this page

## SYNOPSIS [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/ConvertTo-NTAccountOrSID\#synopsis "Direct link to SYNOPSIS")

Convert between NT Account names and their security identifiers (SIDs).

## SYNTAX [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/ConvertTo-NTAccountOrSID\#syntax "Direct link to SYNTAX")

### NTAccountToSID [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/ConvertTo-NTAccountOrSID\#ntaccounttosid "Direct link to NTAccountToSID")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
ConvertTo-NTAccountOrSID -AccountName <String> [<CommonParameters>]

```

### SIDToNTAccount [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/ConvertTo-NTAccountOrSID\#sidtontaccount "Direct link to SIDToNTAccount")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
ConvertTo-NTAccountOrSID -SID <String> [<CommonParameters>]

```

### WellKnownName [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/ConvertTo-NTAccountOrSID\#wellknownname "Direct link to WellKnownName")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
ConvertTo-NTAccountOrSID -WellKnownSIDName <String> [-WellKnownToNTAccount] [<CommonParameters>]

```

## DESCRIPTION [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/ConvertTo-NTAccountOrSID\#description "Direct link to DESCRIPTION")

Specify either the NT Account name or the SID and get the other.
Can also convert well known sid types.

## EXAMPLES [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/ConvertTo-NTAccountOrSID\#examples "Direct link to EXAMPLES")

### EXAMPLE 1 [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/ConvertTo-NTAccountOrSID\#example-1 "Direct link to EXAMPLE 1")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
ConvertTo-NTAccountOrSID -AccountName 'CONTOSO\User1'

```

Converts a Windows NT Account name to the corresponding SID

### EXAMPLE 2 [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/ConvertTo-NTAccountOrSID\#example-2 "Direct link to EXAMPLE 2")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
ConvertTo-NTAccountOrSID -SID 'S-1-5-21-1220945662-2111687655-725345543-14012660'

```

Converts a Windows NT Account SID to the corresponding NT Account Name

### EXAMPLE 3 [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/ConvertTo-NTAccountOrSID\#example-3 "Direct link to EXAMPLE 3")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
ConvertTo-NTAccountOrSID -WellKnownSIDName 'NetworkServiceSid'

```

Converts a Well Known SID name to a SID

## PARAMETERS [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/ConvertTo-NTAccountOrSID\#parameters "Direct link to PARAMETERS")

### -AccountName [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/ConvertTo-NTAccountOrSID\#-accountname "Direct link to -AccountName")

The Windows NT Account name specified in <domain><username> format.
Use fully qualified account names (e.g., <domain><username>) instead of isolated names (e.g, <username>) because they are unambiguous and provide better performance.

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Type: String
Parameter Sets: NTAccountToSID
Aliases:

Required: True
Position: Named
Default value: None
Accept pipeline input: True (ByPropertyName)
Accept wildcard characters: False

```

### -SID [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/ConvertTo-NTAccountOrSID\#-sid "Direct link to -SID")

The Windows NT Account SID.

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Type: String
Parameter Sets: SIDToNTAccount
Aliases:

Required: True
Position: Named
Default value: None
Accept pipeline input: True (ByPropertyName)
Accept wildcard characters: False

```

### -WellKnownSIDName [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/ConvertTo-NTAccountOrSID\#-wellknownsidname "Direct link to -WellKnownSIDName")

Specify the Well Known SID name translate to the actual SID (e.g., LocalServiceSid).

To get all well known SIDs available on system: \[Enum\]::GetNames(\[Security.Principal.WellKnownSidType\])

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Type: String
Parameter Sets: WellKnownName

Required: True
Position: Named
Default value: None
Accept pipeline input: True (ByPropertyName)
Accept wildcard characters: False

```

### -WellKnownToNTAccount [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/ConvertTo-NTAccountOrSID\#-wellknowntontaccount "Direct link to -WellKnownToNTAccount")

Convert the Well Known SID to an NTAccount name

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Type: SwitchParameter
Parameter Sets: WellKnownName
Aliases:

Required: False
Position: Named
Default value: False
Accept pipeline input: False
Accept wildcard characters: False

```

### Accepts a string containing the NT Account name or SID. [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/ConvertTo-NTAccountOrSID\#accepts-a-string-containing-the-nt-account-name-or-sid "Direct link to Accepts a string containing the NT Account name or SID.")

## NOTES [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/ConvertTo-NTAccountOrSID\#notes "Direct link to NOTES")

This is an internal script function and should typically not be called directly.

The conversion can return an empty result if the user account does not exist anymore or if translation fails.

[http://blogs.technet.com/b/askds/archive/2011/07/28/troubleshooting-sid-translation-failures-from-the-obvious-to-the-not-so-obvious.aspx](http://blogs.technet.com/b/askds/archive/2011/07/28/troubleshooting-sid-translation-failures-from-the-obvious-to-the-not-so-obvious.aspx)

## File: psappdeploytoolkit.com_docs_3.10.2_reference_functions_Copy-ContentToCache.md

url: "https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-ContentToCache"
title: "Copy-ContentToCache · PSAppDeployToolkit"
---

[Skip to main content](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-ContentToCache#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

This is documentation for PSAppDeployToolkit **3.10.2 (Deprecated)**, which is no longer actively maintained.

For up-to-date documentation, see the **[latest version](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/introduction)** (4.1.0).

Version: 3.10.2 (Deprecated)

On this page

## SYNOPSIS [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-ContentToCache\#synopsis "Direct link to SYNOPSIS")

Copies the toolkit content to a cache folder on the local machine and sets the $dirFiles and $supportFiles directory to the cache path

## SYNTAX [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-ContentToCache\#syntax "Direct link to SYNTAX")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Copy-ContentToCache [[-Path] <String>] [<CommonParameters>]

```

## DESCRIPTION [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-ContentToCache\#description "Direct link to DESCRIPTION")

Copies the toolkit content to a cache folder on the local machine and sets the $dirFiles and $supportFiles directory to the cache path

## EXAMPLES [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-ContentToCache\#examples "Direct link to EXAMPLES")

### EXAMPLE 1 [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-ContentToCache\#example-1 "Direct link to EXAMPLE 1")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Copy-ContentToCache -Path 'C:\Windows\Temp\PSAppDeployToolkit'

```

## PARAMETERS [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-ContentToCache\#parameters "Direct link to PARAMETERS")

### -Path [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-ContentToCache\#-path "Direct link to -Path")

The path to the software cache folder

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Type: String
Parameter Sets: (All)
Aliases:

Required: False
Position: 1
Default value: "$configToolkitCachePath\$installName"
Accept pipeline input: False
Accept wildcard characters: False

```

### CommonParameters [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-ContentToCache\#commonparameters "Direct link to CommonParameters")

This cmdlet supports the common parameters: -Debug, -ErrorAction, -ErrorVariable, -InformationAction, -InformationVariable, -OutVariable, -OutBuffer, -PipelineVariable, -Verbose, -WarningAction, and -WarningVariable. For more information, see [about\_CommonParameters](https://go.microsoft.com/fwlink/?LinkID=113216).

## INPUTS [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-ContentToCache\#inputs "Direct link to INPUTS")

## OUTPUTS [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-ContentToCache\#outputs "Direct link to OUTPUTS")

## NOTES [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-ContentToCache\#notes "Direct link to NOTES")

This function is provided as a template to copy the toolkit content to a cache folder on the local machine and set the $dirFiles directory to the cache path.
This can be used in the absence of an Endpoint Management solution that provides a managed cache for source files, e.g.
Intune is lacking this functionality whereas ConfigMgr includes this functionality.
Since this cache folder is effectively unmanaged, it is important to cleanup the cache in the uninstall section for the current version and potentially also in the pre-installation section for previous versions.
This can be done using \[Remove-File -Path "$configToolkitCachePath$installName" -Recurse -ContinueOnError $true\]

## RELATED LINKS [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-ContentToCache\#related-links "Direct link to RELATED LINKS")

[https://psappdeploytoolkit.com](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/)

- [DESCRIPTION](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-ContentToCache#description)
- [EXAMPLES](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-ContentToCache#examples)

[Skip to main content](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-File#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

This is documentation for PSAppDeployToolkit **3.10.2 (Deprecated)**, which is no longer actively maintained.

For up-to-date documentation, see the **[latest version](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/introduction)** (4.1.0).

Version: 3.10.2 (Deprecated)

On this page

## SYNOPSIS [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-File\#synopsis "Direct link to SYNOPSIS")

Copy a file or group of files to a destination path.

## SYNTAX [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-File\#syntax "Direct link to SYNTAX")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Copy-File [-Path] <String[]> [-Destination] <String> [-Recurse] [-Flatten] [-ContinueOnError <Boolean>]
 [-ContinueFileCopyOnError <Boolean>] [-UseRobocopy <Boolean>] [-RobocopyParams <String>]
 [-RobocopyAdditionalParams <String>] [<CommonParameters>]

```

## DESCRIPTION [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-File\#description "Direct link to DESCRIPTION")

Copy a file or group of files to a destination path.

## EXAMPLES [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-File\#examples "Direct link to EXAMPLES")

### EXAMPLE 1 [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-File\#example-1 "Direct link to EXAMPLE 1")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Copy-File -Path "$dirSupportFiles\MyApp.ini" -Destination "$envWinDir\MyApp.ini"

```

### EXAMPLE 2 [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-File\#example-2 "Direct link to EXAMPLE 2")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Copy-File -Path "$dirSupportFiles\*.*" -Destination "$envTemp\tempfiles"

```

Copy all of the files in a folder to a destination folder.

## PARAMETERS [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-File\#parameters "Direct link to PARAMETERS")

### -Path [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-File\#-path "Direct link to -Path")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Position: 1
```

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Position: 2
```

### -UseRobocopy [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-File\#-userobocopy "Direct link to -UseRobocopy")

Use Robocopy to copy files rather than native PowerShell method.
Robocopy overcomes the 260 character limit.
Supports \* in file names, but not folders, in source paths.
Default is configured in the AppDeployToolkitConfig.xml file: $true

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Type: Boolean
Parameter Sets: (All)
Aliases:

Required: False
Position: Named
Default value: $configToolkitUseRobocopy
Accept pipeline input: False
Accept wildcard characters: False

```

### -RobocopyParams [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-File\#-robocopyparams "Direct link to -RobocopyParams")

Override the default Robocopy parameters.
Default is: /NJH /NJS /NS /NC /NP /NDL /FP /IS /IT /IM /XX /MT:4 /R:1 /W:1


## File: psappdeploytoolkit.com_docs_3.10.2_reference_functions_Copy-FileToUserProfiles.md

---
url: "https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-FileToUserProfiles"
title: "Copy-FileToUserProfiles · PSAppDeployToolkit"
---

[Skip to main content](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-FileToUserProfiles#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

This is documentation for PSAppDeployToolkit **3.10.2 (Deprecated)**, which is no longer actively maintained.

For up-to-date documentation, see the **[latest version](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/introduction)** (4.1.0).

Version: 3.10.2 (Deprecated)

On this page

## SYNOPSIS [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-FileToUserProfiles\#synopsis "Direct link to SYNOPSIS")

Copy one or more items to a each user profile on the system.

## SYNTAX [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-FileToUserProfiles\#syntax "Direct link to SYNTAX")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Copy-FileToUserProfiles [-Path] <String[]> [[-Destination] <String>] [-Recurse] [-Flatten]
 [-UseRobocopy <Boolean>] [-RobocopyAdditionalParams <String>] [-ExcludeNTAccount <String[]>]
 [-ExcludeSystemProfiles <Boolean>] [-ExcludeServiceProfiles <Boolean>] [-ExcludeDefaultUser]
 [-ContinueOnError <Boolean>] [-ContinueFileCopyOnError <Boolean>] [<CommonParameters>]

```

## DESCRIPTION [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-FileToUserProfiles\#description "Direct link to DESCRIPTION")

Copy one or more items to a each user profile on the system.

## EXAMPLES [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-FileToUserProfiles\#examples "Direct link to EXAMPLES")

### EXAMPLE 1 [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-FileToUserProfiles\#example-1 "Direct link to EXAMPLE 1")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Copy-FileToUserProfiles -Path "$dirSupportFiles\config.txt" -Destination "AppData\Roaming\MyApp"

```

Copy a single file to C:\\Users<UserName>\\AppData\\Roaming\\MyApp for each user.

### EXAMPLE 2 [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-FileToUserProfiles\#example-2 "Direct link to EXAMPLE 2")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Copy-FileToUserProfiles -Path "$dirSupportFiles\config.txt","$dirSupportFiles\config2.txt" -Destination "AppData\Roaming\MyApp"

```

Copy two files to C:\\Users<UserName>\\AppData\\Roaming\\MyApp for each user.

### EXAMPLE 3 [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-FileToUserProfiles\#example-3 "Direct link to EXAMPLE 3")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Copy-FileToUserProfiles -Path "$dirFiles\MyApp" -Destination "AppData\Local" -Recurse

```

Copy an entire folder to C:\\Users<UserName>\\AppData\\Local for each user.

### EXAMPLE 4 [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-FileToUserProfiles\#example-4 "Direct link to EXAMPLE 4")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Copy-FileToUserProfiles -Path "$dirFiles\.appConfigFolder" -Recurse

```

Copy an entire folder to C:\\Users<UserName> for each user.

## PARAMETERS [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-FileToUserProfiles\#parameters "Direct link to PARAMETERS")

### -Path [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-FileToUserProfiles\#-path "Direct link to -Path")

The path of the file or folder to copy.

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Type: String[]
Parameter Sets: (All)
Aliases:

Required: True
Position: 2
Default value: None
Accept pipeline input: True (ByValue)
Accept wildcard characters: False

```

### -Destination [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-FileToUserProfiles\#-destination "Direct link to -Destination")

The path of the destination folder to append to the root of the user profile.

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Type: String
Parameter Sets: (All)
Aliases:

Required: False
Position: 3
Default value: None
Accept pipeline input: False
Accept wildcard characters: False

```

### -Recurse [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-FileToUserProfiles\#-recurse "Direct link to -Recurse")

Copy files in subdirectories.

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Type: SwitchParameter
Parameter Sets: (All)
Aliases:

Required: False
Position: Named
Default value: False
Accept pipeline input: False
Accept wildcard characters: False

```

### -Flatten [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-FileToUserProfiles\#-flatten "Direct link to -Flatten")

Flattens the files into the root destination directory.

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Type: SwitchParameter
Parameter Sets: (All)
Aliases:

Required: False
Position: Named
Default value: False
Accept pipeline input: False
Accept wildcard characters: False

```

### -UseRobocopy [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-FileToUserProfiles\#-userobocopy "Direct link to -UseRobocopy")

Use Robocopy to copy files rather than native PowerShell method.
Robocopy overcomes the 260 character limit.
Only applies if $Path is specified as a folder.
Default is configured in the AppDeployToolkitConfig.xml file: $true

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Type: Boolean
Parameter Sets: (All)
Aliases:

Required: False
Position: Named
Default value: $configToolkitUseRobocopy
Accept pipeline input: False
Accept wildcard characters: False

```

### -RobocopyAdditionalParams [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-FileToUserProfiles\#-robocopyadditionalparams "Direct link to -RobocopyAdditionalParams")

Default is: $null

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Type: String[]

```

### -ExcludeSystemProfiles [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-FileToUserProfiles\#-excludesystemprofiles "Direct link to -ExcludeSystemProfiles")

### -ContinueOnError [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-FileToUserProfiles\#-continueonerror "Direct link to -ContinueOnError")

Continue if an error is encountered.
This will continue the deployment script, but will not continue copying files if an error is encountered.
Default is: $true.

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Type: Boolean
Parameter Sets: (All)
Aliases:

Required: False
Position: Named
Default value: True
Accept pipeline input: False
Accept wildcard characters: False

```

### -ContinueFileCopyOnError [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Copy-FileToUserProfiles\#-continuefilecopyonerror "Direct link to -ContinueFileCopyOnError")

Continue copying files if an error is encountered.
This will continue the deployment script and will warn about files that failed to be copied.
Default is: $false.

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Type: Boolean
Parameter Sets: (All)
Aliases:

Required: False
Position: Named
Default value: False
```

## File: psappdeploytoolkit.com_docs_3.10.2_reference_functions_Execute-MSI.md

---
url: "https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-MSI"
title: "Execute-MSI · PSAppDeployToolkit"
---

[Skip to main content](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-MSI#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

This is documentation for PSAppDeployToolkit **3.10.2 (Deprecated)**, which is no longer actively maintained.

For up-to-date documentation, see the **[latest version](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/introduction)** (4.1.0).

Version: 3.10.2 (Deprecated)

On this page

## SYNOPSIS [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-MSI\#synopsis "Direct link to SYNOPSIS")

Executes msiexec.exe to perform the following actions for MSI & MSP files and MSI product codes: install, uninstall, patch, repair, active setup.

## SYNTAX [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-MSI\#syntax "Direct link to SYNTAX")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Execute-MSI [[-Action] <String>] [-Path] <String> [[-Transform] <String>] [[-Parameters] <String>]
 [[-AddParameters] <String>] [-SecureParameters] [[-Patch] <String>] [[-LoggingOptions] <String>]
 [[-private:LogName] <String>] [[-WorkingDirectory] <String>] [-SkipMSIAlreadyInstalledCheck]
 [-IncludeUpdatesAndHotfixes] [-NoWait] [-PassThru] [[-IgnoreExitCodes] <String>]
 [[-PriorityClass] <ProcessPriorityClass>] [[-ExitOnProcessFailure] <Boolean>] [[-RepairFromSource] <Boolean>]
 [[-ContinueOnError] <Boolean>] [<CommonParameters>]

```

## DESCRIPTION [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-MSI\#description "Direct link to DESCRIPTION")

Executes msiexec.exe to perform the following actions for MSI & MSP files and MSI product codes: install, uninstall, patch, repair, active setup.

If the -Action parameter is set to "Install" and the MSI is already installed, the function will exit.

Sets default switches to be passed to msiexec based on the preferences in the XML configuration file.

Automatically generates a log file name and creates a verbose log file for all msiexec operations.

Expects the MSI or MSP file to be located in the "Files" sub directory of the App Deploy Toolkit.
Expects transform files to be in the same directory as the MSI file.

## EXAMPLES [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-MSI\#examples "Direct link to EXAMPLES")

### EXAMPLE 1 [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-MSI\#example-1 "Direct link to EXAMPLE 1")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Execute-MSI -Action 'Install' -Path 'Adobe_FlashPlayer_11.2.202.233_x64_EN.msi'

```

Installs an MSI

### EXAMPLE 2 [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-MSI\#example-2 "Direct link to EXAMPLE 2")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Execute-MSI -Action 'Install' -Path 'Adobe_FlashPlayer_11.2.202.233_x64_EN.msi' -Transform 'Adobe_FlashPlayer_11.2.202.233_x64_EN_01.mst' -Parameters '/QN'

```

Installs an MSI, applying a transform and overriding the default MSI toolkit parameters

### EXAMPLE 3 [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-MSI\#example-3 "Direct link to EXAMPLE 3")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
[PSObject]$ExecuteMSIResult = Execute-MSI -Action 'Install' -Path 'Adobe_FlashPlayer_11.2.202.233_x64_EN.msi' -PassThru

```

Installs an MSI and stores the result of the execution into a variable by using the -PassThru option

### EXAMPLE 4 [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-MSI\#example-4 "Direct link to EXAMPLE 4")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Execute-MSI -Action 'Uninstall' -Path '{26923b43-4d38-484f-9b9e-de460746276c}'

```

Uninstalls an MSI using a product code

### EXAMPLE 5 [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-MSI\#example-5 "Direct link to EXAMPLE 5")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Execute-MSI -Action 'Patch' -Path 'Adobe_Reader_11.0.3_EN.msp'

```

Installs an MSP

## File: psappdeploytoolkit.com_docs_3.10.2_reference_functions_Execute-MSP.md

---
url: "https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-MSP"
title: "Execute-MSP · PSAppDeployToolkit"
---

[Skip to main content](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-MSP#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

This is documentation for PSAppDeployToolkit **3.10.2 (Deprecated)**, which is no longer actively maintained.

For up-to-date documentation, see the **[latest version](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/introduction)** (4.1.0).

Version: 3.10.2 (Deprecated)

On this page

## SYNOPSIS [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-MSP\#synopsis "Direct link to SYNOPSIS")

Executes an MSP file using the same logic as Execute-MSI.

## SYNTAX [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-MSP\#syntax "Direct link to SYNTAX")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Execute-MSP [-Path] <String> [[-AddParameters] <String>] [<CommonParameters>]

```

## DESCRIPTION [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-MSP\#description "Direct link to DESCRIPTION")

Reads SummaryInfo targeted product codes in MSP file and determines if the MSP file applies to any installed products
If a valid installed product is found, triggers the Execute-MSI function to patch the installation.
Uses default config MSI parameters.
You can use -AddParameters to add additional parameters.

## EXAMPLES [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-MSP\#examples "Direct link to EXAMPLES")

### EXAMPLE 1 [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-MSP\#example-1 "Direct link to EXAMPLE 1")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Execute-MSP -Path 'Adobe_Reader_11.0.3_EN.msp'

```

### EXAMPLE 2 [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-MSP\#example-2 "Direct link to EXAMPLE 2")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Execute-MSP -Path 'AcroRdr2017Upd1701130143_MUI.msp' -AddParameters 'ALLUSERS=1'

```

## PARAMETERS [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-MSP\#parameters "Direct link to PARAMETERS")

### -Path [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-MSP\#-path "Direct link to -Path")

Path to the msp file

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Type: String
Parameter Sets: (All)
Aliases: FilePath

Required: True
Position: 1
Default value: None
Accept pipeline input: False
Accept wildcard characters: False

```

### -AddParameters [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-MSP\#-addparameters "Direct link to -AddParameters")

Additional parameters

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Type: String
Parameter Sets: (All)
Aliases:

Required: False
Position: 2
Default value: None
Accept pipeline input: False
Accept wildcard characters: False

```

## File: psappdeploytoolkit.com_docs_3.10.2_reference_functions_Execute-Process.md

---
url: "https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-Process"
title: "Execute-Process · PSAppDeployToolkit"
---

[Skip to main content](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-Process#__docusaurus_skipToContent_fallback)

This is documentation for PSAppDeployToolkit **3.10.2 (Deprecated)**, which is no longer actively maintained.

For up-to-date documentation, see the **[latest version](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/introduction)** (4.1.0).

Version: 3.10.2 (Deprecated)

On this page

## SYNOPSIS [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-Process\#synopsis "Direct link to SYNOPSIS")

Execute a process with optional arguments, working directory, window style.

## SYNTAX [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-Process\#syntax "Direct link to SYNTAX")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Execute-Process [-Path] <String> [[-Parameters] <String[]>] [-SecureParameters]
 [[-WindowStyle] <ProcessWindowStyle>] [-CreateNoWindow] [[-WorkingDirectory] <String>] [-NoWait] [-PassThru]
 [-WaitForMsiExec] [[-MsiExecWaitTime] <Int32>] [[-IgnoreExitCodes] <String>]
 [[-PriorityClass] <ProcessPriorityClass>] [[-ExitOnProcessFailure] <Boolean>] [[-UseShellExecute] <Boolean>]
 [[-ContinueOnError] <Boolean>] [<CommonParameters>]

```

## DESCRIPTION [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-Process\#description "Direct link to DESCRIPTION")

Executes a process, e.g.
a file included in the Files directory of the App Deploy Toolkit, or a file on the local machine.
Provides various options for handling the return codes (see Parameters).

## EXAMPLES [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-Process\#examples "Direct link to EXAMPLES")

### EXAMPLE 1 [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-Process\#example-1 "Direct link to EXAMPLE 1")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Execute-Process -Path 'uninstall_flash_player_64bit.exe' -Parameters '/uninstall' -WindowStyle 'Hidden'

```

If the file is in the "Files" directory of the App Deploy Toolkit, only the file name needs to be specified.

### EXAMPLE 2 [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-Process\#example-2 "Direct link to EXAMPLE 2")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Execute-Process -Path "$dirFiles\Bin\setup.exe" -Parameters '/S' -WindowStyle 'Hidden'

```

### EXAMPLE 3 [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-Process\#example-3 "Direct link to EXAMPLE 3")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Execute-Process -Path 'setup.exe' -Parameters '/S' -IgnoreExitCodes '1,2'

```

### EXAMPLE 4 [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-Process\#example-4 "Direct link to EXAMPLE 4")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Execute-Process -Path 'setup.exe' -Parameters "-s -f2`"$configToolkitLogDir\$installName.log`""

```

Launch InstallShield "setup.exe" from the ".\\Files" sub-directory and force log files to the logging folder.

### EXAMPLE 5 [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-Process\#example-5 "Direct link to EXAMPLE 5")

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Execute-Process -Path 'setup.exe' -Parameters "/s /v`"ALLUSERS=1 /qn /L* `"$configToolkitLogDir\$installName.log`"`""

```

Launch InstallShield "setup.exe" with embedded MSI and force log files to the logging folder.

## PARAMETERS [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-Process\#parameters "Direct link to PARAMETERS")

### -Path [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-Process\#-path "Direct link to -Path")

Path to the file to be executed.
If the file is located directly in the "Files" directory of the App Deploy Toolkit, only the file name needs to be specified.
Otherwise, the full path of the file must be specified.
If the files is in a subdirectory of "Files", use the "$dirFiles" variable as shown in the example.

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Type: String
Parameter Sets: (All)
Aliases: FilePath

Required: True
Position: 1
Default value: None
Accept pipeline input: False
Accept wildcard characters: False

```

### -WindowStyle [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-Process\#-windowstyle "Direct link to -WindowStyle")

Style of the window of the process executed.
Options: Normal, Hidden, Maximized, Minimized.
Default: Normal.
Note: Not all processes honor WindowStyle.
WindowStyle is a recommendation passed to the process.
They can choose to ignore it.
Only works for native Windows GUI applications.
If the WindowStyle is set to Hidden, UseShellExecute should be set to $true.


UseShellExecute should be set to $false.

### -ExitOnProcessFailure [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-Process\#-exitonprocessfailure "Direct link to -ExitOnProcessFailure")

Specifies whether the function should call Exit-Script when the process returns an exit code that is considered an error/failure.

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Type: Boolean
Parameter Sets: (All)
Aliases:

Required: False
Position: 8
Default value: True
Accept pipeline input: False
Accept wildcard characters: False

```

### -UseShellExecute [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-Process\#-useshellexecute "Direct link to -UseShellExecute")

Specifies whether to use the operating system shell to start the process.
$true if the shell should be used when starting the process; $false if the process should be created directly from the executable file.

The word "Shell" in this context refers to a graphical shell (similar to the Windows shell) rather than command shells (for example, bash or sh) and lets users launch graphical applications or open documents.
It lets you open a file or a url and the Shell will figure out the program to open it with.
The WorkingDirectory property behaves differently depending on the value of the UseShellExecute property.
When UseShellExecute is true, the WorkingDirectory property specifies the location of the executable.
When UseShellExecute is false, the WorkingDirectory property is not used to find the executable.
Instead, it is used only by the process that is started and has meaning only within the context of the new process.
If you set UseShellExecute to $true, there will be no available output from the process.

Default: $false

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Type: Boolean
Parameter Sets: (All)
Aliases:

Required: False
Position: 9
Default value: False
Accept pipeline input: False
Accept wildcard characters: False

```

### -ContinueOnError [​](https://psappdeploytoolkit.com/docs/3.10.2/reference/functions/Execute-Process\#-continueonerror "Direct link to -ContinueOnError")

Continue if an error occured while trying to start the process.
Default: $false.

```codeBlockLines_Fl5M
Type: Boolean
Parameter Sets: (All)
Aliases:

Required: False
Position: 10
Default value: False
Accept pipeline input: False
Accept wildcard characters: False

```

For more information, see [about\_CommonParameters](https://go.microsoft.com/fwlink/?LinkID=113216).
